# WAL Disk Format\\n2: \\n3: This document describes the official Prometheus WAL format.\\n4: \\n5: The write ahead log operates in segments that are numbered and sequential,\\n6: and are limited to Here is a comprehensive overview of the implementation:\\n\\n## WAL Segment Creation and Rotation\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** contains the core WAL implementation:\\n- **CreateSegment()** and **OpenWriteSegment()** create and open new WAL segments\\n- **NextSegment()** and **NextSegmentSync()** manage segment rotation by creating a new segment when the current one is full, then asynchronously or synchronously closing the previous segment\\n- **Segment struct** represents a single WAL segment file with methods for writing and syncing\\n- **WL struct** is the main write-ahead log manager that tracks the active segment, manages paging (32KB pages), and handles compression\\n- **Log()** method writes records to the WAL, automatically triggering segment rotation when records are too large to fit in the remaining space\\n- **Segments()** and **listSegments()** enumerate all WAL segments and maintain sequential ordering\\n- **LastSegmentAndOffset()** returns the last segment number and the offset position within it\\n\\n## WAL Record Encoding\\n\\n**tsdb/record/record.go** implements record encoding/decoding for the WAL:\\n- **Encoder struct** with methods:\\n  - **Series()** encodes series records (metric labels with unique IDs)\\n  - **Samples()** encodes float sample records (timestamp-value pairs indexed by series ref)\\n  - **Tombstones()** encodes deletion records for deleted series\\n  - **Exemplars()** encodes exemplar records with labels\\n  - **HistogramSamples()** encodes classic histogram samples\\n  - **FloatHistogramSamples()** encodes native float histogram samples\\n  - **CustomBucketsHistogramSamples()** and **CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples()** for histograms with custom buckets\\n  - **MmapMarkers()** encodes memory-mapped chunk markers for out-of-order data\\n  - **Metadata()** encodes metric metadata (type, unit, help text)\\n- **Decoder struct** with methods to decode each record type from bytes\\n- **RefSeries, RefSample, RefTombstone, RefExemplar** structs hold encoded record data\\n- Records are delta-encoded for compression (timestamps and refs stored as deltas from the first record)\\n\\n## WAL Reading\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/reader.go** provides sequential reading of WAL segments:\\n- **Reader** reads WAL records from segment files\\n- **NewReader()** creates a reader for a set of segments\\n- Handles record fragments that span page boundaries\\n- Detects corruption and returns **CorruptionErr** with segment and offset information\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go** provides live tailing of actively-written WAL segments:\\n- **LiveReader** reads from an io.Reader (e.g., a segment being actively written)\\n- **NewLiveReader()** creates a live reader for real-time WAL monitoring\\n- Useful for remote write to tail WAL data as it's being written\\n- Handles EOF gracefully to allow waiting for more data\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/watcher.go** monitors WAL segments and processes records:\\n- **Watcher** watches the WAL directory for new segments and sends records to a WriteTo sink\\n- Used by remote write to consume WAL records\\n- Processes series, samples, exemplars, and metadata records\\n- Provides metrics for record reading progress\\n\\n## WAL Repair\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** includes corruption repair:\\n- **Repair()** method handles WAL corruption by:\\n  1. Taking a **CorruptionErr** that specifies the segment and byte offset of corruption\\n  2. Deleting all segments after the corrupted one\\n  3. Rewriting the corrupted segment, removing all records after the corruption point\\n  4. Creating a new segment to continue writing\\n- This discards corrupted data but preserves all valid records up to the corruption\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go** implements checkpoint creation to truncate old WAL data:\\n- **Checkpoint()** function creates a compacted checkpoint of WAL segments in a given range [from, to]\\n- **CheckpointStats** tracks how many series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, and metadata records were kept vs dropped\\n- **LastCheckpoint()** finds the most recent checkpoint directory and index\\n- **DeleteCheckpoints()** deletes old checkpoints below a given index\\n- **DeleteTempCheckpoints()** cleans up incomplete checkpoint directories\\n- Checkpoints are stored in directories named checkpoint.N (e.g., checkpoint.5) with the same segmented format as the WAL\\n- Allows filtering of series to keep via a keep() callback function\\n- Only includes data newer than a specified mint (minimum timestamp)\\n- This enables discarding old WAL files that are no longer needed, reducing storage requirements\\n\\n## Integration with Head Block\\n\\n**tsdb/head_wal.go** and **tsdb/head_append.go** integrate WAL with the in-memory head block:\\n- WAL replay on startup to reconstruct in-memory state\\n- Recording of series, samples, tombstones when they are added\\n- Tracking of WAL expiries for deleted series\\n\\n**tsdb/db.go** integrates WAL at the database level:\\n- Creates and manages the WAL instance\\n- Handles WAL replay and repair on startup\\n- Triggers checkpoint creation during compaction\\n- Manages WAL truncation when blocks are compacted\\n\\n**tsdb/agent/db.go** provides an agent-specific WAL implementation for remote-write use cases:\\n- Customized WAL that removes data immediately after remote write\\n- Repair and checkpoint functionality specific to agent mode\\n\\nAll these components work together to provide durable, recoverable storage of recent metrics data in the
